  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b32fb103-9617-4fc6-9ded-8700af210435'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">See a picture on a helicopter, you see that thing at the back sticking out, that’s the tail. If you see that thing that moves left and right on the ta<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">See a picture on a helicopter, you see that thing at the back sticking out, that’s the tail. If you see that thing that moves left and right on the tail (it looks like it’s part of the tail, but it moves) is the rudder.<br />Don’t worry if you don’t understand airplanes have been my passion for over 10 years<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

The reason Dan isnt with Amy is becasue they got mad at each other ( Amy was talking rudly about their parents). Since they have found out they were Madgrgals they have changed alot.... I think so far that this book has been very boring and almost no adventure at all. Even though the writer puts a picture in my mind its not one thats very exicting.. Still I wonder...   <span id="freeText6304969628936016251" style="display:none">This book was mainly that sometimes the reward is worth the risk. In this book and series the reward is nothing short of the chance of world domination, the reward making you the most powerful person in the world. In this book they are in china, tracing down members of the Qing dynasty and their Cahill heritage. Dan gets separated and has to find his way back to Amy and Nellie, while avoiding certain members of the family and the social services. They go through many dangers and as usual dodge death many times. But they still stay in the hunt, showing time and time again that they think the rewards of the hunt are worth the risks for them.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1543926520654159992">After the bit of a cop-out ending of the previous book, we finally get to see the fallout of Dan and Amy's Cahill branch revelation. And it's...pretty angsty, for no real reason, so far. They're convinced that, as Madrigals, they're some sort of monsters. And, just when they really need each other the most, they're split up, Amy and Nellie together, and Dan alone in Shanghai.<br/><br/>Until he runs into Jonah Wizard.<br/><br/>Every few books seems to focus on humanizing a Cahill member, and this time we see Jonah a</span>
  <span id="freeText1543926520654159992" style="display:none">After the bit of a cop-out ending of the previous book, we finally get to see the fallout of Dan and Amy's Cahill branch revelation. And it's...pretty angsty, for no real reason, so far. They're convinced that, as Madrigals, they're some sort of monsters. And, just when they really need each other the most, they're split up, Amy and Nellie together, and Dan alone in Shanghai.<br /><br />Until he runs into Jonah Wizard.<br /><br />Every few books seems to focus on humanizing a Cahill member, and this time we see Jonah and his non-Cahill father in more detail. It's actually pretty interesting, and pretty relevant to me, from having watched parents of other musical performers push their kids to what seems a dangerous degree in their performances.<br /><br />The history of the Cahill family continues getting more ridiculous, this time claiming the last Chinese Dynasty was part of a Cahill branch. Which...really? Really? We're going a bit far, at this point.<br /><br />Still, for kids, it will be enjoyable, and I'm looking forward to getting down to the bottom of the 39 Clues mystery in the last three books of the original series.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1683666333284095786">It was about average for the series, better than a few but not one of the most amazing. I enjoyed the way this book used history, weaving it into the story more than lecturing. There were just a few too many coincidences, even based on the scale of this juvenile/YA series.   <span id="freeText1683666333284095786" style="display:none">It was about average for the series, better than a few but not one of the most amazing. I enjoyed the way this book used history, weaving it into the story more than lecturing. There were just a few too many coincidences, even based on the scale of this juvenile/YA series. I was especially annoyed by the way Dan found a clue at the beginning, it was just too too easy. Also, some of the language was just not how kids think or speak; at one point Dan muses about the unstoppable juggernaut that killed both of his parents. I know he's smart, but the whole paragraph was out of an adult novel. Overall, the mystery and emotional content were good. And as usual, it left me excited to read the next book. We're getting close to the end! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4696903043068386592">A journey to the east! Again. But this time to China. Without knowing where to go and what to look for, Amy and Dan headed for China with a simple and indefinite lead. The only way to find each other was to follow the clue hunt.<br/> But what I most liked in the book was The Great Wall of China being described. A structure with thousands of years' history. The place where I want</span>
  <span id="freeText4696903043068386592" style="display:none">A journey to the east! Again. But this time to China. Without knowing where to go and what to look for, Amy and Dan headed for China with a simple and indefinite lead. On top of that, they've got separated in the most populated country, and been deceived by Jonah Wizard to get what he want. The only way to find each other was to follow the clue hunt.<br /> But what I most liked in the book was The Great Wall of China being described. A structure with thousands of years' history. The place where I want to go most. &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="4696903043068386592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2328428758" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2328428758" />
    <a title="Ocean Weeks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31359202-ocean-weeks"><img alt="Ocean Weeks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484879963p2/31359202.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2328428758?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ocean Weeks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ocean Weeks" href="/user/show/31359202-ocean-weeks">Ocean Weeks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31359202-ocean-weeks?shelf=middlegrade">middlegrade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2328428758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4668063595692656960">"As the race to find the 39 Clues builds to its explosive finish, Amy and Dan must explore an ancient culture and steal a Clue guarded by thousands of the world's best-trained soldiers. It's the most dangerous Clue search yet. As their enemies crowd in, Amy and Dan find themselves separated for the first time ever. The choice lies before them - find the next Clue, or find their way back to each other."<br/><br/>I decided to copy and paste the synopsis to the book as I didn't want to risk spoiling anyone f</span>
  <span id="freeText4668063595692656960" style="display:none">"As the race to find the 39 Clues builds to its explosive finish, Amy and Dan must explore an ancient culture and steal a Clue guarded by thousands of the world's best-trained soldiers. It's the most dangerous Clue search yet. As their enemies crowd in, Amy and Dan find themselves separated for the first time ever. The choice lies before them - find the next Clue, or find their way back to each other."<br /><br />I decided to copy and paste the synopsis to the book as I didn't want to risk spoiling anyone for this book if they hadn't already read it, or started reading the series. <br /><br />In this novel, there is quite a different dynamic from the rest of the books in the series. We see different players interacting more. For example, we get to see a different side of Dan and Amy's cousin Jonah Wizard, a gangster/rapper/television star and see more of what he's like besides the slightly dimwitted and obnoxious image he portrays. We get to see him interact more with Dan, and we see Amy and Nellie interact way more. Which is especially interesting due to the fact that it's rare that Amy and Dan interact with anyone without their sibling being in the same vicinity. I think this was definitely a fresh idea after similar situations of Dan and Amy working through problems, puzzles and codes together. I like that we get to see the pair of them develop more on their own and experience new growth without growing apart. If anything, their bond only gets stronger through these new issues and transitions happening. Amy's doubts about her parents and herself after the discovery of which branch she and her little brother belong to are extreme but fair in the sense that, if I were in her shoes, I feel as though I would be thinking similar things. However, I definitely understand Dan's denial and his wanting to keep the wool pulled over his eyes for a little longer. It's clear he doesn't want to think of his parents as anything less than angels and he refuses to see or admit that they might have done thing that were wrong, and spends a lot of time angry at his older sister for admitting such things. <br /><br />This series is a blessing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4668063595692656960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1020613928380492274">I fall more in love with this series every second.<br/>I love including snippets I like....sue me. :)<br/>***<br/>"Let's see, the doohickey of supreme whatchamacallit is over <i>there</i>-"<br/>"Hall of Supreme Harmony," Amy corrected.<br/>"-so I bet the Janus crest should be somewhere in <i>this</i> section, over by the whatchamacallit of tranquil thingamajig."<br/>"Palace of Tranquil Longevity," Amy supplied.<br/> (Don't tell me you guys didn't crack a smile here :)<br/>***<br/>My favourite part in the whole book :<br/><br/>His opponent's grip disintegrated. <i>"D</i></span>
  <span id="freeText1020613928380492274" style="display:none">I fall more in love with this series every second.<br />I love including snippets I like....sue me. :)<br />***<br />"Let's see, the doohickey of supreme whatchamacallit is over <i>there</i>-"<br />"Hall of Supreme Harmony," Amy corrected.<br />"-so I bet the Janus crest should be somewhere in <i>this</i> section, over by the whatchamacallit of tranquil thingamajig."<br />"Palace of Tranquil Longevity," Amy supplied.<br /> (Don't tell me you guys didn't crack a smile here :)<br />***<br />My favourite part in the whole book :<br /><br />His opponent's grip disintegrated. <i>"Dan?"</i><br /><i>"Amy?"</i><br />"Oh, God!" Nellie dropped the crowbar she was just about to bring down on Dan's head.<br />The two Cahills scrambled up, each one goggling as if the sight of the other was a mirage. Then they were together in an ecstatic bear hug.<br />"Cut it out!" Dan complained. "You're strangling me!" But he didn't loosen his grip on his sister.<br />Amy had been so worried for so long that the sudden evaporation of tension left her boneless. If she let go, she probably would have collapsed in a heap. "I thought I'd lost you! Just like we lost Mom and Dad!"<br />"Why didn't you look for me?" Dan babbled.<br />"We did! We never stopped!"<br />"Oh, yeah? Then what are you doing here?"<br />"Well, it must have been exactly the right place!" Amy snapped. "You showed up, didn't you?"<br />"I caught the Holts on TV!" Dan pulled away. "Stop yelling at me! I missed you so much! I thought I 'd never see you again!"<br /><br />***<br />I think this book was monumental in making Dan and Amy realise just how much they needed each other. And those parts where Dan was actually admitting that he missed her and not making a wisecrack about it; the part where they hugged for the first time in the WHOLE series....it means it's serious how much they care and love each other...and how serious this situation was. They are one word, literally inseparable: <i> DanandAmy....AmyandDan </i></span>

<div id="review_2252716745" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2252716745" />
    <a title="Patrick Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71365907-patrick-campbell"><img alt="Patrick Campbell" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2252716745?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick Campbell" href="/user/show/71365907-patrick-campbell">Patrick Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2252716745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18214060617887004204">The book The Emperor’s Code by Gordon Korean was kind of a let down for a thirty nine clues book. The Cahills are the richest and most powerful family on the planet. They find out the next clue is in China, the most populated country in the world. After long arguments and tragic events the family gets split up. Without each other Amy and Dan will have much more of a challenge finding the clue. Will they find it? Will they survive? <br/><br/>For a thirty nine clues book it was not that good. It had lots of</span>
  <span id="freeText18214060617887004204" style="display:none">The book The Emperor’s Code by Gordon Korean was kind of a let down for a thirty nine clues book. The Cahills are the richest and most powerful family on the planet. They find out the next clue is in China, the most populated country in the world. After long arguments and tragic events the family gets split up. Without each other Amy and Dan will have much more of a challenge finding the clue. Will they find it? Will they survive? <br /><br />For a thirty nine clues book it was not that good. It had lots of detail, although they focused on things that were not important to the plot. Also even though the plot was unique and creative I really disliked it. I wanted to stop reading every 5 pages and got bored with it because there was no action or climax. There were absolutely 0 twists or turns in the story to surprise you. Overall the book was pretty bad and was not too interesting.<br /><br />I would not recommend this book to anybody. I would feel bad to recommend a book to somebody and them not enjoy it. This is exactly how I feel with this particular book. Please do not waste your time by reading The Emperors Code.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18214060617887004204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('C5ySC7w8qNvdayMrIpBJXNlquyOK0tmwKYbVCX9MXBju1JtTXiqBH5Iij/92g8gy9TyfvtV58hARMwoLf044QA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('s8YfqZxk1N5LFK0/NWa3n1l7NexgM9aygQWDsI2MfkZWjhbxfnL9GgRdAethdTbxdS0RcT+Y/RK5sFyyjY4aHg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9167101573501279870">Korman wrote his first book, "This Can't be Happening at Macdonald Hall", when he was 12 years old, for a coach who suddenly found himself teaching 7th grade English. He later took that episode and created a book out of it, as well, in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q="The%20Sixth%20Grade%20Nickname%20Game"' title='"The Sixth Grade Nickname Game"' rel='nofollow noopener'>"The Sixth Grade Nickname Game"</a>, wherein Mr. Huge was based on that 7th grade teacher.<br/><br/>Korman moved to New York City, where he studied film and film writing. While i</span>
  <span id="freeText9167101573501279870" style="display:none">Korman wrote his first book, "This Can't be Happening at Macdonald Hall", when he was 12 years old, for a coach who suddenly found himself teaching 7th grade English. He later took that episode and created a book out of it, as well, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=&quot;The%20Sixth%20Grade%20Nickname%20Game&quot;" title="&quot;The Sixth Grade Nickname Game&quot;" rel="nofollow noopener">"The Sixth Grade Nickname Game"</a>, wherein Mr. Huge was based on that 7th grade teacher.<br /><br />Korman moved to New York City, where he studied film and film writing. While in New York, he met his future wife; they now live in Long Island with their three children.<br /><br />He has published more than 50 books.</span>
